Poor Autumn Cocoon Harvest in Jiangsu and Zhejiang: Shanghai Factories Fear Shortage of Raw Materials; Hope That the Zhejiang Unified Committee Will Offer Spring Cocoons at a Reasonable Price; Overseas Silk Market Suddenly Rises Yesterday and Trading Becomes Active 126

Due to the poor autumn cocoon harvest in Jiangsu and Zhejiang this year, coupled with the large-scale purchases by the Wuxi Yongtai Silk Factory, Shanghai silk factories are experiencing a shortage of raw materials and are hoping that the Zhejiang Unified Committee will transfer the stored spring cocoons to the factories at a reasonable price. The overseas silk market suddenly rose yesterday. The details are as follows:

Yongtai Silk Factory Purchases in Large Quantities

The autumn cocoon harvest in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces this year has been poor due to the yellowing of mulberry leaves and weather conditions. The cocoons collected by silk factories and leftover cocoon merchants are difficult to profit from due to poor reeling and breakage. However, the Wuxi Yongtai Silk Factory, opened by silk tycoon Xue Shou Xuan, purchased in large quantities and offered high cocoon prices. At the same time, it purchased dried cocoons from small factories and leftover cocoon merchants. Small factories and leftover cocoon merchants believed that they would not be able to profit at the current prices of silk factories, so they were willing to sell the dried cocoons.

Shanghai Factories Fear Shortage of Raw Materials

Because of the poor autumn cocoon harvest this year and the large-scale purchases by the Wuxi Yongtai Silk Factory, Shanghai silk factories are experiencing a shortage of raw materials. Currently, forty-eight factories, including Xinglun and Xiangcheng, are operating with 11,000 machines. It is expected that after another month, they will all stop working due to lack of raw materials. Those with sufficient raw materials can only maintain operations until the end of the lunar year. Now, in order to maintain the livelihood of tens of thousands of workers, we hope that the Zhejiang Silk Unified Committee will transfer the four to five thousand dan of spring cocoons collected this year, which are stored in various warehouses, at a reasonable price to alleviate the cocoon shortage for various manufacturers. Since the beginning of autumn, the prices of overseas Chinese silk trade have gradually declined. Silk factories are unwilling to sell the reeled silk because it is difficult to profit from it. They are waiting and seeing, which has led to a sharp decrease in exports of Chinese silk. Domestic silk factories are also experiencing reduced sales due to the tense situation. However, yesterday, the prices of overseas Chinese silk suddenly rose, from US$1.62 to US$1.66, an increase of about 20 yuan per dan, which led to a smoother silk trading. Whether it can be sustained is difficult to predict.

Japanese Troops Inside the Japan Brewery in Zhabei Come and Go Without a Fixed Pattern; Patrol Teams Still Seen Coming and Going on Jiangwan Road 135

The Japanese troops stationed inside the Japan Brewery at the end of Huayuan Street in Zhabei withdrew once on the 19th, and then returned to station in the afternoon of the same day. According to the investigation, the reason for their withdrawal and return was that among the more than 100 Japanese soldiers stationed there, one Japanese soldier suddenly died of an infectious disease in the morning. Therefore, the Japanese troops stationed there were ordered to withdraw completely, disinfect all parts of the factory inside and out, and even transport all military supplies out for disinfection. After completion, more than 40 troops were sent to guard the factory. At dawn yesterday, more than 130 Japanese troops, divided into several military vehicles and loaded with military supplies, drove to station. Soon, another 70 Japanese troops drove away from the factory. After 3:00 p.m., another 60 to 70 Japanese troops left the factory, and did not return until evening. Therefore, the number of Japanese troops stationed in the Japan Brewery has been reduced to 30 to 40 people, coming and going without a fixed pattern and unpredictable. As for the Jiangwan Road area in the city, Japanese patrol teams were still seen coming and going yesterday morning. The situation on North Sichuan Road is also the same as before.

Lawyer Li Man, the bankruptcy administrator of Minghua Bank, sued the bank's president Zhang Gangbo, assistant president Yu Dequn, and assistant manager Zhen Man for breach of trust. This has been reported in previous newspapers. It is now learned that Zhang Gangbo has been sentenced to five years in prison by the Qingdao District Court. However, Zhang could not be transferred to Shanghai at this time, so he ruled that the trial would be temporarily suspended.

Consumption of Rouge and Perfume

The United States Ranks First in Imports

The Figures for Nine Months Are Alarming

In the first nine months of this year, the import figures for cosmetics, perfumes, rouge, snow creams, tooth powders, and toothpastes in Shanghai totaled 377,248 gold units, equivalent to approximately 829,945 yuan in national currency. The Datong News Agency reporter has checked the classified figures with the Statistics Office of the International Trade Bureau, as follows:

Rouge and Perfume

In the first nine months of this year, the total import of rouge, perfume, and other unlisted cosmetics in Shanghai was 172,414 gold units. In the first nine months of this year, the import of snow creams in Shanghai was only in the previous month, totaling 21,750 gold units. The total import of snow creams was 67,410 gold units, only imported in the previous month, totaling 11,921 gold units. In the first nine months of this year, the total import of tooth powders and toothpastes in Shanghai was 94,815 gold units, only imported in the previous month, totaling 8,938 gold units.

Importing Countries

The countries of origin for the above rouge, perfume, and other unlisted cosmetics (total for nine months) are: France 39,507 gold units, Germany 16,190 gold units, England 39,149 gold units, Japan 16,305 gold units, the United States 60,673 gold units, and other countries 452 gold units.

No Rain in Autumn Makes Farming Difficult Farmers Hope for Rain Soil Dryness Affects Crop Growth Pests Thrive, Growth Still Insufficient 141

Since the beginning of summer this year, the climate has been mild and the wind and rain have been favorable, so crops such as cotton, rice, soybeans, etc. have grown vigorously and have had good harvests. Farmers are generally happy. However, since the beginning of autumn, the weather has been dry for nearly forty days without rain. At this time of autumn plowing, the lack of rain has caused the soil to dry out, making plowing difficult. Autumn crops such as wheat, rapeseed, and broad beans need to be sown urgently, so farmers are very eager for rain. Moreover, the vegetables planted in the fields are also affected by the dry soil, making it difficult for them to grow. The pests on the vegetable leaves are multiplying day by day. Farmers in neighboring villages, although irrigating and catching insects, are still unable to grow enough vegetables, so the price of vegetables on the market is also more expensive than in previous years.

This Newspaper's Workers Prepare to Commemorate Ge Guanfu 142

Ge Guanfu, a member of the Shanghai Newspaper Workers' Union, worked in the news typesetting department of this newspaper and was a loyal worker. Unfortunately, he was brutally murdered by his wife on the afternoon of the 13th of this month. The tragic news has shocked the public, and newspaper colleagues are particularly indignant. In addition to separately requesting a strict investigation of the murderer to avenge Ge, the workers of this newspaper, because Ge was a close colleague, had always been diligent and conscientious, and was amiable and approachable, were indeed a model worker. Now that he has suddenly died tragically, they are even more saddened. It is now planned to hold a memorial meeting on a fixed date to comfort the deceased. Everything is being actively prepared.

China Merchants Bureau's Freight and Passenger Transport Increases Sharply Creating a New Record in Recent Years 143

Due to various factors such as the limitations of the state-owned China Merchants Bureau, its business has been declining day by day. All those concerned about state-owned shipping are worried about it. Since the reorganization in the spring of this year, the authorities have been determined to rectify the situation, and there has been a gradual trend of prosperity. The bureau's freight and passenger transport from February to June of this year has increased, averaging about 26% compared to the same months of last year. This has been disclosed in the newspapers. It is now learned that the bureau's freight and passenger transport revenue for July increased by more than 11% compared to the same month last year. The freight and passenger transport in August increased even more sharply, with the total revenue for the month being 755,451.22 yuan, compared to 509,868.6 yuan in the same month last year, an increase of 245,582.96 yuan, an increase rate of 48%. The reason for the rapid progress of its business and the creation of a new record in recent years is, of course, the hard work of the personnel in charge of the business at the general and branch offices after careful rectification, as well as the support of the Chinese people for the government's reorganization plan, resulting in their willingness to support and assist. If the bureau continues to work tirelessly and actively expand its routes, it will surely add a different color to China's shipping industry in the future.

Ningbo Fellow Association Investigates Zhang Mingde 144

The Ningbo Shanghai Fellow Association sent a letter to the Police Department of the Public Concession yesterday, stating: "Regarding the case reported by our association member Lin Haizhou, Haizhou operates the Wufeng Wax Paper Factory at No. 4 Chengyin Lane, Fangxie Road, with a distribution office at No. 6 Jinchun Lane, No. 215 Meibaige Road. At 9:00 PM on the 17th of this month, two strangers suddenly came and claimed to be detectives from the Chengdu Road Police Station. They said that someone was pursuing your debt and asked you to go to the police station for questioning. Haizhou was shocked to hear this and was forced to leave. Two more people were waiting at the entrance of the lane. They boarded a car parked at the entrance and drove to the Chengdu Road Police Station. The car stopped in an open space. A long-faced man in a suit claimed that 500 yuan was needed to settle the matter. His words were extremely threatening. Haizhou, an ordinary person, did not know the inside story and repeatedly pleaded to reduce it to 300 yuan. He returned to No. 6 Jinchun Lane in the same car and paid 150 yuan in cash and a check for 150 yuan dated the 18th. The next morning at 1:00 AM, Haizhou, accompanied by lawyer Ye Xiabiao, reported the incident to the Xinzha Police Station for investigation. At 2:00 PM on the same afternoon, a Wu surnamed person brought the check to Haizhou for cashing. He was asked to wait a moment, and then he went to the Xinzha Police Station to invite a Western detective and detectives to come. They apprehended Wu, who confessed that he was working for Zhang Mingde, the detective chief of the Chengdu Road Police Station. Although the Xinzha Police Station has detained Zhang Mingde and his accomplice Yao Zijia, and Haizhou has identified them without error, Mingde and others have also confessed directly, but no public prosecution has been heard to this day, which is very strange. Therefore, we hereby write to your association to uphold the traditional purpose of protecting fellow villagers and grant assistance. We hereby request the Police Department of the Public Concession to thoroughly investigate and order the Xinzha Police Station to initiate a public prosecution as soon as possible, without delay, in order to uphold the law and prevent corruption."

New Beijing Ship's Workers Draw Lots for Retention The Day Before Yesterday 50 Workers Retained 96 Workers Dismissed 145

The issue of the British Taikoo Company's New Beijing Ship reducing the number of workers in the middle cabin department was decided by drawing lots the day before yesterday. The details are as follows:

Drawing Lots the Day Before Yesterday

After the Taikoo Company's New Beijing Ship was grounded, the Tongzhou Ship was renamed and put into service. The two ships had a total of 176 workers in the middle cabin department. The company authorities claimed that the ship was too small to accommodate them, so they proposed a reduction. After negotiations by the Seamen's Union, they agreed to retain 80 workers. At 10:00 AM the day before yesterday, a drawing of lots for retention was held at the Middle Cabin Office on Wangyima Lane. Secretary Wang Ji of the General Union, Section Chief Tu Yalun, Branch Director Peng Bowei, and Cheng Yongming, as well as all the workers, were present.

50 Retained

Of the 176 people, 59 did not participate in the drawing (one had already left, 18 had addictions and illnesses, 10 did not trust the union, 15 workers were from the Tongzhou Ship, and 15 were New Beijing group leaders and cadres). 117 people participated in the drawing. Of the 117 blank papers, 50 had the word "retain" written on them, and the rest had the word "dismiss". Each person drew a paper in turn. Those who drew a paper with the word "retain" would continue to serve, and those who drew a paper with the word "dismiss" would be dismissed. A total of 50 people were retained, and 96 were dismissed.

Severance Pay Given

The dismissed workers were given three months of severance pay by the business manager, totaling 48 yuan. After negotiations by the union, they were given an additional 52 yuan. The retained workers were given 20 yuan each for living expenses. The workers also contributed 60 yuan each, totaling 165.384 yuan per dismissed worker. 120 yuan was paid in advance at the time, and the remaining balance was to be collected on the 21st. By 4:00 PM, all the procedures had been completed. The retained workers continued to serve, and the rest left the ship.

Please Appoint a Mediator

For the sake of their unemployed colleagues, the workers' representatives decided on the following five measures: 1. Priority employment for dismissed workers, 2. Replacements can be made by dismissed workers, 3. The income of the retained workers will be evenly distributed among the dismissed workers, etc. However, these measures were not approved, so yesterday the workers specially sent Tu Zhenbiao and Jiang Fuji to the Ningbo Fellow Association to request Chu Qiaqing and the All Zhejiang Association to act as mediators and reduce the pain of unemployment.

Concession Health Authorities Provide Relief for Russian Children with Schistosomiasis 149

According to the Public Works Department Health Department, this summer, 55 Russian Boy Scouts from this city camped in a nearby area, surrounded by rice paddies and ponds. The water contained a large number of schistosomiasis-causing worms. Upon returning, 50 of the 55 children were infected with schistosomiasis. The Public Works Department Health Department considers the matter serious and has adopted a cooperative approach with the French Concession health authorities to prevent the spread of the disease. Since the families of the Russian children are mostly poor, and the thiophene agent for treating schistosomiasis is very expensive, they are unable to afford it. Therefore, they have requested the authorities to find ways to provide relief.

Theft and Copying of Lamp Manufacturing Methods - Continued Hearing of a Chinese Lawsuit - Defendants Admit to Copying - Further Investigation of the Case Pending 150

Zhu Jianlin from Nanhui and Liu Ziyi from Shandong developed the Hua Yi battery safety lamp. Recently, they discovered that Gao Yushan, the manager of the Guangming Electric Lamp Factory in Dunren Lane, Avenue Dubail, French Concession, and Wu Zhirong, the supervisor, had stolen and copied the original formula that Zhu and others had registered and publicly announced with the Ministry of Industry. They illegally imitated the lamp in an attempt to profit from it. They hired lawyer Zou Shengzu to file a lawsuit with the Second Special District Court. A hearing was held once, but because the second defendant, Wu Zhirong, and the witness, Dai Fuyuan, did not appear, the hearing was rescheduled. All details have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, at the prosecutor's request, the people involved were brought to the court. Judge Zhang Minsheng continued the trial in the Second Criminal Court. First, Gao Yushan was questioned about whether the Guangming Electric Lamp Factory was a cooperative venture with others or solely operated by him. Gao replied that it was a sole proprietorship. The finished products, originally stored at No. 1 Faxing Lane, Liyuan Road, had been shipped to Hubei and Henan. The judge asked if there were any documents proving business transactions, and Gao replied no. Next, Wu Zhirong testified, aged 45, stating that he did indeed copy the Hua Yi formula, and that he copied it from the Industry Gazette to show Gao Yushan. Then, the witness Dai Fuyuan testified, aged 41, from Taixing, engaged in the cloth business. He did not know Gao Yushan or Wu Zhirong. He knew them through Chen Wenfeng, his former employer. Wu Zhirong told him that there was a person named Bai Yushan who had a better lamp manufacturing method than Hua Yi. He provided a formula, made an agreement, and asked Dai to experiment with it. Dai, not knowing chemistry, did not dare show it to a third party because he was bound by an oath of damnation. Later, Wu asked him to go to lawyer Pin Xiehua to invite Gao Yushan to negotiate. Wu gave the formula to Gao, and Guangming gradually succeeded because of it. Also, because Dai was the Taixing sales agent for Hua Yi, Wu instructed him to instigate a third party, Wang, to sign another contract, fabricate facts, and file lawsuits against Hua Yi with the municipal government, the Ministry of Industry, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, and the Municipal Party Headquarters to undermine Hua Yi. The draft was written by Wu Zhirong himself (evidence can be verified). Dai only submitted the document to the Social Affairs Bureau because Wu was an employee of the Social Affairs Bureau and he did not dare send it to other agencies. The judge asked if he had gone to the Guangming factory in July, and Dai replied no. The lease for the Guangming factory's building will not begin until November. After verifying the testimonies, the court concluded that further investigation was needed and adjourned the hearing to the 27th.

Yin Chunbao, 32, from Zhenjiang, opened the Ouya Clock and Watch Shop on North Sichuan Road. At the same time, he also worked as a clock and watch repairman at An Kang Foreign Firm (specializing in clocks and watches) in the Sassoon Building on Nanjing Road. All damaged clocks and watches, as well as new clocks and watches shipped from abroad, had to be handed over to Yin for repair and inspection. Under questioning, Yin confessed that he had successively embezzled many clocks and watches from the foreign firm. A portion of them was pawned for 300 yuan to Chen Yingsheng, an employee of the Zhenda Pawnshop at No. 465 Avenue Edward VII (Yin's father-in-law). The detectives went to recover five gold pocket watches, two clocks, and two wristwatches, totaling 2,415 yuan. Because further investigation was needed to determine if Yin had embezzled other goods, he requested a postponement of the hearing. Questioning Yin, he confessed that the clocks and watches recovered were taken from An Kang. After Judge Feng Shide verified the confession, he ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody and postponed the hearing for one week.

Book Industry Guild Holds Meeting, Passes Industry Regulations 157

This city is a gathering place for the publishing industry, but it has always upheld the spirit of mutual respect, maintaining the division of labor and cooperation for the national cultural and educational cause, without encroachment or disruption. However, in the past decade, more and more people have entered this field, and the future of the book industry has become increasingly prosperous. People have long thought about having formal regulations that are easy to follow. At the members' meeting in 1934, members such as Sao Ye Shan Fang proposed formulating industry regulations. However, the scope of the book industry is quite broad, and the nature of books varies between new and old, and the printing methods vary between letterpress and lithography. Furthermore, the same new books are divided into textbooks and miscellaneous books. The methods are not entirely the same, and the costs are also different. Uniformity is ultimately seen as forced adaptation. Three years have passed, and after repeated discussions, no results have been achieved. On July 19th of this year, at the members' meeting, the old matter was brought up again. It was decided to organize a drafting committee to draft industry regulations. Nineteen companies were selected as committee members, including Commercial Press, Zhonghua Book Company, World Book Company, Datong Book Company, Tianming Book Company, Zhengzhong Book Company, Guangyi Book Company, Jinzhang Book Company, Huiwen Book Company, Beixin Book Company, New China Book Company, Shanggu Book Company, Wenrui Book Company, Tianma Book Company, Life Book Company, Yadong Book Company, Author Book Company, Guangming Book Company, and Shanghai Magazine. Each company sent one representative to attend, including Zhang Shuliang, Wang Zhuoqing, Lu Gaoyi, Luo Wuyai, Ding Xiaoxian, Lu Pinqin, Wei Bingrong, Yu Yiqing, Xu Baolu, Li Zhiyun, Lu Youbai, Ding Yunheng, Zhou Airu, Guo, Yan Changyan, Wang Mengzou, Huang Buxiang, Wang Zicheng, Zhang Jing, and others. Zhang Shuliang was elected as chairman, Ding Xiaoxian as secretary, and Commercial Press, Author Book Company, Huiwen Book Company, Life Book Company, and Shanghai Magazine were designated as drafting committee members. After two meetings, a draft was completed. After five meetings of the entire drafting committee, it was passed on August 18th, consisting of 53 draft articles. It was submitted to the executive committee, which borrowed the Shanghai Municipal Higher Society Hall at 1:00 PM on the 18th of this month to convene a general meeting of all members. Representatives from the Municipal Party Headquarters, He Yuanming, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Yuan Hongjun, attended, along with 35 member representatives. As the quorum was not reached, Lu Feibohong, Zhang Shuliang, Wei Bingrong, Lu Gaoyi, and Zhou Airu served as the presidium. After the superiors' representatives gave instructions according to protocol, Zhang Shuliang, chairman of the drafting committee, reported on the drafting process. Then, the draft industry regulations, as well as the amendments to the draft proposed by the executive committee and member representative Zhang Xichen, were discussed in detail. The meeting was lively and lasted for more than five hours, finally concluding at 8:00 PM. A total of 55 industry regulations were established, and everyone applauded to celebrate the success. After submitting the regulations to the competent authorities for approval, they will be officially announced and implemented on a scheduled date. Furthermore, given the recent rampant piracy and disguised piracy, the executive committee proposed levying a three-month monthly donation as a temporary special donation to hire a lawyer and staff to handle piracy investigations, which was also unanimously approved.

Young women who are determined to return to school but cannot afford to continue their studies can quickly go to the school to register for the examination.

Also accused was Gu Erkang of the Dongfang Daily. The first instance judgment fined both newspapers 200 yuan and prohibited their distribution. Wu Nonghua and others disagreed with the verdict and hired two major lawyers, Xu Jie and Wang Liwu, to file an appeal according to law. A hearing was also held on the case. Yesterday was the date of the verdict, the original verdict was overturned, and the newspapers were allowed to continue publishing as usual, with only a fine of 50 yuan.

Xu Zhengui Reports to the Defense Corps, Uses Paper Money Scheme to Capture Extortionists, Jiang Songshi and Huang Abao Also from Shaoxing, Orders Jiang to Write Handwriting Similar to the Threatening Letter 172

Xu Zhengui, a Shaoxing native who runs the Ronghua Dyeing and Weaving Factory, resides at No. 1 Tongxing Lane, behind Lujia浜, Nanshi. Recently, he suddenly received two threatening letters from bandits. The wording was very intense, demanding $1,000 in silver dollars. The money was to be wrapped in newspaper at 6:00 AM on the 20th, and placed at the corner of the third street lamp wall next to the Jiuxin Enamel Factory on Zhizao局 Road, with the character "You" written on the wall as a sign. Someone would come to retrieve it. If reported to the police, they would harm his son, and so on. After receiving the letter, Xu immediately had his son, Deshun, notify the Defense Corps, explaining the situation. The third team of the Corps sent four members, along with platoon leader Chong Muqing, to accompany Xu Deshun to the designated location at the appointed time to wait in ambush. Meanwhile, Xu Deshun prepared $1,000 in paper money as instructed. Before long, two men arrived, peering around. Just as they were about to take the money, the Defense Corps members rushed forward and apprehended them. They were sent, along with the $1,000 in paper money, to the Ximen Sub-Bureau. One identified himself as Jiang Songshi, 23 years old, and the other as Huang Abao, 22 years old, both from Shaoxing. The rest of their statements were vague. Jiang was then ordered to write numbers to compare the handwriting, which was indeed similar to the handwriting in the threatening letter. As the matter involved extortion, it was deemed a serious case. Orders were given to prepare a document to be submitted to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

The Shen Bao National Goods Special

Words of Contribution

Home Visits and the Responsibilities of Housewives 173

— Yang An

Visiting housewives is the most important task of the national goods movement. The Shanghai National Goods Movement Joint Association has been doing this for three weeks now, and the volunteers have visited 530 households. The ladies' tireless spirit and patient and persuasive attitude are truly admirable. However, during the visits, they have endured ridicule and sarcasm. Sometimes, they are barred by the doorman, and sometimes, they are insulted by the servants. They may even be met with cold indifference from the mistresses. Yet, they do not lose heart or become passive. They continue to do the work they should be doing.

Doormen, servants, and even old maids and maids have not received education. They do not know what is lovable or unlovable about a country. They only understand the power of the powerful, and act arrogantly in the kitchen and servants' quarters. Let alone other things, even if the country is lost, they will still be someone's slaves. They do not know what national goods are, and they do not have national goods in their minds. We should not blame them. Instead, we should pity them. It is a pity that they lack knowledge and humanity. Therefore, we should not expect or resent them.

However, the mistresses or young mistresses seem to have forgotten their own status. You are clearly Chinese, and you should use Chinese goods. Why do you like to use foreign goods? Why are you not persistent in your actions? Why do you disregard national goods and indulge in momentary pleasure, using non-national goods? When the female volunteers arrive at your home, you put on airs and act arrogant. You either say you do not have time to see guests, or you say you do not want to talk to people. This kind of behavior seems too cold-blooded and lacking in enthusiasm. Let us tell you honestly:

The work of these volunteers is partly for the benefit of the national goods factories, and partly for the benefit of these housewives. It allows you to seek advice, solicit your opinions on national goods, and explore your feelings about using them. Based on the opinions expressed by the 530 housewives, the association has asked the national goods factories to make earnest improvements in order to meet the expectations of many housewives. I remember that several housewives admitted that national goods are good, but the prices are not cheap. Some housewives buy things at national goods companies, but they feel that the store clerks do not pay enough attention to politeness. The female volunteers have told the association all of this so that they can discuss improvements. Therefore, if you do not speak, that is one thing. But if you speak, all the national goods manufacturers are willing to adopt your opinions. This is a great opportunity to express your opinions, which is hard to come by. Why do you reject people from a thousand miles away when they come to your door? In this light, how can Shanghai be considered civilized, enlightened, or patriotic? How can there be enthusiastic men and women? If the housewives are like this, then one can imagine what the children and servants are like. I am now telling the housewives: from now on, when female volunteers come to your door, you must receive them sincerely and discuss matters earnestly. You must express your dissatisfaction with national goods, and you must also say what you admire about national goods. This will help to create communication and unity between producers and consumers, and the national goods industry will have hope.

A Glimpse of the Anle Woolen Textile Factory 174

— Zhen Sheng

Clothing is an important part of people's daily lives. Take wool yarn, for example. In the past, brands like "Bee Brand" almost monopolized the Chinese wool yarn market, with a history of over 120 years, accounting for 90% of imported wool yarn. How could the annual loss be less than tens of millions? "Small leaks sink great ships." This is a truly enormous loss! In recent years, domestic industrialists, seeing that promoting national goods is essential to saving the country, have established larger-scale wool yarn factories, such as Zhanghua and Anle in Shanghai, and Haijing in Tianjin, among three or four others. Through their efforts to improve quality and the enthusiastic promotion by compatriots, they have been able to recover a significant portion of these rights and interests. Take the Anle Woolen Textile Factory as an example. Its "Beauty Brand" and "Money Brand" have long been popular throughout the country. This year, they have launched a new "Hero Brand" special grade yarn. The fiber content is exceptionally long, making it durable. It can be worn until it is dirty and then retied. Even after five or six reties, there is no damage. It is cheaper and better than imported goods, if not surpassing them. The appearance of this "Hero Brand" is directly intended to counter the dumping of "Bee Brand," so that it will eventually disappear from the national goods market.

One clear and crisp afternoon, the author was invited by Mr. Deng Zhonghe to visit the factory. The factory is located at No. 34 Route Brenier, and the building is quite magnificent. Director Wang personally guided the tour, explaining the factory's history and sales situation. The entire process of spinning, weaving, and dyeing, including "carding, sorting, splitting, twisting, packaging, boxing," "sizing, spinning, weaving," and "bleaching, dyeing, drying," was explained step by step. According to Director Wang, after the January 28th Incident in Shanghai, the market was extremely depressed. Anle, after a year of preparation, opened despite everything. Everyone, holding a spirit of sacrifice, buried themselves in hard work and struggled for five years. Fortunately, they have not been affected by the "depression," and have laid a foundation. The capital has increased from one million yuan to one million one hundred thousand yuan. Currently, business is still progressing rapidly. The entire factory has 20-30 spinning machines and hundreds of weaving machines. There are nearly a thousand employees. For raw materials, domestic sources are Jiang浙, Shandong, Tianjin, Guanneiwai wool producing areas. Foreign sources are Siberia, Australia. The new "Hero Brand" sales are very good. The previous "Beauty Brand" of grade A, the "Money Brand" of grade B, and the four and six-strand wool yarn are already in short supply, sold throughout the provinces. Even remote provinces and Southeast Asian islands are buying in large quantities. But they are not complacent. They are currently planning to add new factory buildings, purchase more machinery, and expand their scope, until foreign goods disappear and national goods are on the rise. This spirit of revitalizing national products and dedicating themselves to industry is truly admirable!

The City Chamber of Commerce National Goods Exhibition in the Midst of Extended Exhibition Period 175

— Sheng

(Feature) I heard that the National Goods Exhibition hosted by the City Chamber of Commerce had been extended, so I quickly went for a visit. These days, the autumn weather is clear and crisp, and the exhibition venue is very lively. There are also foreign ladies and gentlemen who are flowing in and out with us, like the autumn tide and autumn clouds. The first impression is that although trade has national boundaries, the main points are the quality of the goods and the suitability of the prices. Moreover, this place gathers the first-class factories in the country and displays the first-class products in the country.

We were surprised and delighted to see that the light bulbs from the Ya Pu Er Electric Factory and the sofas and cushions from the An Mian Si Mattress Factory were constantly surrounded by clusters of foreign customers, who seemed happy to buy them.

Everyone knows that the manufacturing of toys can influence children's thinking. The toys from Kang Yuan Factory are truly exquisite, like the "Rising Monkey" and "Rotating Car," which everyone likes.

In recent years, China's new drug industry has shown a tendency to catch up. The Xin Ya Pharmaceutical Factory and the Sino-French and Sino-Western pharmacies, which participated in the exhibition, have all received general attention. It is said that business at the venue has been satisfactory. Representatives of foreign pharmaceutical factories in Shanghai have also frequently come to offer their compliments, especially expressing unspeakable admiration for Xin Ya's products.

At the venue, I ran into a famous artist who was examining the display spirit and color matching of various factories. He praised the displays of Yi Feng Enamel Factory, Hua Cheng Tobacco Company, Hua Sheng Electric Factory, Tai Kang Biscuit Factory, and Tiger Brand Yong'an Hall, saying that they were very good at beautification and aesthetics.

The front of the venue gathers the nine famous factories, which are China Chemical Industry Society, Mei Ya Silk Weaving Factory, China Enamel Factory, Hua Fu Hat Factory, Wu He Weaving Factory, Hong Xin Dyeing and Weaving Factory, Ya Guang Bakelite Factory, China First Knitting Factory, and Yi Xin Toothbrush Factory. These nine factories, in Shanghai or, more broadly, in China, are planting the seeds of today's national goods prosperity. In the year after the "September 18th Incident," they boldly held an organized National Goods Store on Nanjing Road, below the tail of foreign goods. The China National Goods Company, which now occupies a prominent position on Nanjing Road, was also born from these nine factories.

Finally, we feel that the City Chamber of Commerce Commodity Display Hall, which initiated this exhibition, is the definite base camp for Shanghai's national goods activities. They have the spirit of fifteen years of struggle and the determination to work continuously. Yesterday, the major factories participating in the exhibition jointly made a rectangular plaque and held a plaque presentation ceremony to thank Mr. Wang Xiaoxiang, the president of the exhibition, and Mr. Xu Xiaochu, the vice president. We know that plaques are a kind of souvenir in the old society, but in the future, hanging them in the display hall will have great historical significance.

The Flower of National Goods 176

— Meng Zhao

National Spirit! Some countries choose plum blossoms or chrysanthemums as their national flower, taking their meaning from their ability to endure frost, stand firm on ice, and be solitary and fragrant! Now, with the launch of the female volunteers of national goods, I can call them "The Flower of National Goods"! Their aspirations and actions are pure and undefiled by foreign goods, like plum and chrysanthemum flowers standing out in the wind and snow! Unyielding! National goods have their own value! And word of mouth is everything! The flower of national goods has supreme glory. Do not misunderstand that the female volunteers, representing the national flower, are flowers in a vase! Vases can only be admired! This has long been criticized. Now, the female volunteers and ladies can do solid work with their feet on the ground! Practical work! This is truly representing the flower of national goods! And they are confident of achieving complete and great results! The writer hopes that Ms. Xu and others, in their lively visits, and interactions with family men and women, will bring some dignity to their exquisite and smiling posture, so that people will respect them, and indirectly believe in national goods. Then, wouldn't the mission and responsibility of the flower of national goods be great and heavy?

Spring and Autumn

Mourning Mr. Lu Xun 178

— Ji Ping

The death of Mr. Lu Xun is the fall of a giant star in the Chinese literary world, and the loss of a warrior in the cultural world. We stand on the same literary position and cannot help but express our deepest grief! Although I personally only met Mr. Lu Xun once, I can hardly claim to have any personal relationship with him. However, I have read quite a few of his writings, translations, compilations, editions, and books that he edited over the past decade. His scholarly demeanor, the transcendence of his thoughts, and his contributions to the cultural movement are all admirable and worthy of praise. Even in his later years, he maintained a consistent spirit and engaged in writing, unlike most people who become disheartened and their thoughts decline after middle age. Therefore, he was able to capture the belief of countless readers and spread the seeds of literary revolution. In recent years, especially after the national crisis, the power generated by his writings has been very strong and has won the sympathy of the general public. This is indeed his special talent. He can be considered the first person among contemporary Chinese literary giants!

It is often said that "literati have no integrity," so society generally looks down on so-called literati. Mr. Lu Xun was unique in his ability to be sober while others were drunk, and clear while others were muddy. He had a firm and unwavering heart and had his own central views when commenting on private matters or discussing national affairs. He was right when it was right, and wrong when it was wrong. This selfless and uncompromising spirit is also worthy of being a model for us literati. Now, there are too many clever people in China, but there are too few people who speak the truth, discuss justice, and have backbone. What I feel most sad about while mourning Mr. Lu Xun is this.

Respectfully Mourning Mr. Lu Xun 179

— Fei

Mr. Lu Xun's creative career is not only in China, but also in the world, and it has long been well-established. We do not need to add more praise. But Mr. Lu Xun's greatness should not only be in his incomparably sublime works, which accurately reflect our era and will become eternally immortal works, but also in his lifelong spirit of going straight ahead, never retreating, "being strong towards life, struggling towards death" (in the preface to "Life and Death Field"), always being firm and unyielding, and waging a tenacious struggle against all old forces and evil forces. He has always stood on the front line of the era, fighting fiercely for our new society and new humanity. Such a great warrior of the era, from the publication of his "Diary of a Madman" and "The True Story of Ah Q" to his recent participation in the national salvation front, his battle history has never been dim. The clear and bright battles run through his entire life and become the only leader of our advancing cultural front. Today, the sudden death of such a great warrior is an irreparable loss to our vast youth and social masses! From now on, we will no longer be able to see or hear the valuable teachings of this leader of the cultural advance front!

From the Xinhai Revolution to the recent national salvation movement, the greatest influence on our culture and youth's thinking was Mr. Liang Qichao before the Xinhai Revolution, Mr. Hu Shi in the May Fourth era, and Mr. Lu Xun from the May Fourth through the May Thirtieth to the recent period. Undoubtedly, he has directly and indirectly dominated the entire cultural advance front and is the only giant who has influenced the thinking of the vast youth masses! Many warriors of the era have retreated halfway, but only Mr. Lu Xun has never retreated for a moment, leading more youth who came later to fight fiercely for a new society and new humanity! He should be the unparalleled greatest giant of our era, and this is certain to be determined in history without doubt.

After mourning Mr. Lu Xun, the sole leader of our cultural front, with a heart full of sorrow, let us accept the valuable legacy he left behind, follow in his footsteps, and fight more bravely for a new society and new humanity!

"Talent of the East Gate" 180

— Wo Fo

In the present, everything old seems to have fallen, but only the "talent" is still unshakable and receives people's worship, love, and praise. Just look at those poets, writers, and artists who have long hair, are unkempt, and do not pay attention to their appearance. Are they not welcomed everywhere? Then, our Mr. Guo, who is known as the "Talent of the East Gate," has also been a talent for a lifetime and is truly worthy of pride.

Mr. Guo was a "Xiucai" in the late Qing Dynasty, but he got the elegant title of talent not because he passed the Xiucai exam, but because he often read his own proud masterpieces aloud in the streets and often wrote poems on people's white walls. This is something that only a talent can do. Moreover, he fully possessed all the conditions of a talent, so the title of talent could not be rejected. His expression of grief at his father's death further strengthened people's recognition of him as a talent. It turned out that after his father died of illness, he was extremely angry. When he was about to put him in the coffin, he glared angrily, almost pointing to the tip of his father's nose and said: "Why didn't you consider the time of your death first? I have only passed the Xiucai exam now, and you are dead. What glory is there in that? Why didn't you wait for me, let me pass the Zhuangyuan exam, at least get a Tanhua or Jinshi. Then you would return to heaven. Not only would your funeral be much more lavish, but I, as a filial son, could also be generous and show off a bit." He said this, and his father probably knew he was wrong and didn't make a sound. And this made his good name as a talent even more widely known; because he lived in Dongmen (East Gate), he was also called "Talent of the East Gate."

In addition, he spent all his travel expenses when he went to take the exam and went to the teahouse to give lectures on Liaozhai. These were all the true colors of a talent. Although he was only a Xiucai, he said that it was because the imperial examination was abolished, otherwise, he would have definitely gotten a Juren.

For the past twenty years, he has been constantly declining, but his life will not be a problem, because he can go to public places to tell people about the Classic of Mountains and Seas and ghosts. He also secretly does ghostwriting for high school students, so in addition to being a talent, people gave him the nickname "Walking Bookshelf."

Our Mr. Guo has lived his life as a talent like this.

Russian Cuisine 181

— Chen Liang

If in your life, you have not extensively broadened your knowledge of "the art of eating," you will often inevitably reveal an "outsider" air. For example, entering a Sichuan restaurant but not being accustomed to spicy food, entering a Tianjin restaurant but not liking green onions, entering a Cantonese restaurant but disliking the vegetables being undercooked or the rice being too hard, or even entering a Muslim restaurant and demanding to slaughter live eels, the jokes will only become bigger. But "learn a lesson from every fall," living in a metropolis requires learning the "rules" of "eating."

Furthermore, if you have eaten the cuisines of England, France, America... and other countries, or even eaten Indian curry chicken, but have never eaten "Russian cuisine," you cannot be considered to have eaten all the great cuisines in the world, and even less can you be called an "international gourmand." Therefore, mingling in the "foreign concessions," you cannot but eat Russian cuisine.

Even if you are not a poet, but have some poetic sentiment, you always like to stroll along Avenue Joffre, right? If you get hungry from walking and want to eat, you have to find a restaurant. There are no Chinese imperial restaurants or the like, and cafes are too aristocratic, then a Russian restaurant is the best place to go. Perhaps you will hesitate because you don't understand Russian. You can rest assured on this point. Except for the owner and the owner's wife who are truly Russian, the rest of the staff are Chinese compatriots, originally from Yangzhou, amiable and lovely.

Stumbling into the glass door, there is Western music broadcasted on the radio, nude oil paintings on the walls, and vases on the tables with withered flowers. The owner's wife may give you a charming smile, but you can pretend not to see it. Eating a fifty-cent meal, you can ascend the stairs to a refined seat. Asking the waiter for black bread will show that you are an "insider" because you can't find it elsewhere. Although it is harder than white bread, it is richer in vitamins and beneficial to the body. An assorted salad and a half steak. "Outsiders" may order spring chicken, but in reality, they are only gnawing on an old bone. Among them, the most flavorful is undoubtedly "Russian soup," which is plentiful, with cabbage and a large piece of beef, extremely substantial, and usually comes with pudding, fruit, and coffee. Wipe your mouth and stumble out humming the tune of "Tales of the Pavilion."

If a yellow leaf happens to brush your nose, then it will be even more "poetic"!

Correction: In yesterday's "Random Notes on Autumn Interest," the first character was mistakenly printed as "屐" instead of "徒", and the "電" in "電木" was mistakenly printed as "繽". We urgently correct these errors.

Shanghai's Scandalous Life 182

— Guo Lanxin

Paradise is built on sin. The most wicked and abysmal metropolis is considered paradise by many. Before fantasizing about entering paradise, they have already fallen into the abyss of sin.

Shanghai is a paradise built on sin. A scarlet life is a path of depravity into the abyss of sin.

In a scarlet life, there is present laughter, subsequent melancholy, and the taste of sweetness, sourness, bitterness, and spiciness. It is a mixture of money, youth, enjoyment, and depravity. As a result, some pull back from the precipice and turn back to the shore, while others don the cloak of decadence, fall into the abyss of no return, and become sacrificial roles beneath paradise.

In Shanghai, many women, driven by the whip of survival and tempted by the desire for enjoyment, apply rouge and powder, wear bizarre and flamboyant clothes, are skilled at coquetry, and excel at weeping and laughing, selling their youth, bodies, and souls to obtain what they need. Some men use money as a price to buy everything from women to indulge their licentiousness and revelry. This is a buying and selling situation formed by the scandalous lives of both sexes, very much like a marketplace for both sexes.

Both men and women seem very satisfied when the deal is made, but after discovering the shortcomings, disputes inevitably arise. These scandalous events are broadcast in social news from time to time, just like programs on the radio, constantly changing performances.

Grand hotels, grand restaurants, theaters, dance halls, parks, or simply on the streets are places where both sexes perform scandalous dramas. In Shanghai, these places are well-equipped and can arrange the intoxicated men and women very comfortably, but remember not to step into the gates of the court because after passing through that gate, the scandalous drama has reached its final act and unfortunately ends as a tragedy.

Love can change its face. Adultery is love's changed face. The former is welcomed, and the latter is despised. In fact, they are one entity. Behind the sweet words of "I love you" is the fierce appearance of "I accuse you." Gold can buy love, and with alimony, one can commit adultery because people see your alimony and will be tempted and intoxicated to let you commit adultery, like a fish on a hook. But in the end, who is the fish and who is the hook? It is impossible to distinguish.

Brothels have declined, and dance pavilions stand in great numbers. What follows is the rise of escort agencies. Those young women provide escort services for men. In restaurants and hotels, what do they escort? Isn't it just acting out scandalous tricks of both sexes? The day before yesterday, someone called for the escort agency to guide his lover away, which was also a bloody news story.

With strong neighbors pressing the border and the situation being serious, scandalous life in Shanghai continues to be staged. I think that even on the day before the destruction of Great Shanghai, this kind of life will still exist. Paradise? Hell? Shanghai? Is it a scandalous life or a history of sin condensed from blood and tears?

Nanjing Bugs in Shanghai 183

— Pinluo

Shanghai has few insects of all kinds, almost none, but bedbugs are especially numerous, not inferior to mosquitoes in the inland. They suck fat and spread germs, a wicked virtue worthy of the saying "two luminaries of the same era," most hateful. They are great conspirators who "kill like grass without a sound," secretly and furtively engaging in activities in the dark, injuring people with hidden arrows. When the victim wakes up in extreme pain and turns on the light to catch them, they have quietly escaped without a trace—unlike mosquitoes, which make a buzzing sound similar to an airplane when they come, warning us in advance so we can quickly take precautions. Secondly, we can use mosquito nets or gauze cabinets as steel armor to resist mosquito attacks. But we have no way to deal with bedbugs, and we can only await death! Although science is now all-powerful and medicines are complete, there are "Flytox," "Fly Killer," bedbug powder, and other... various extremely powerful new weapons, but they have never been able to subdue bedbugs. They still run rampant, arrogant and reckless! Because their reproductive power is strong and fast, and they hide especially secretly, it is impossible for a small amount of medicine to universally eliminate them. Even if you poison a small part entrenched in the bedding, they can still crawl over from the cracks in the wall of the neighboring room, or cleverly detour and jump down from the roof, trying to gorge their greedy mouths and satisfy their desires before leaving. Thus, human power and pleasure are exhausted! This year, I adopted the only secret recipe passed down from generation to generation, "catch diligently," unable to sleep peacefully, and killing without mercy. For three or four months, the average number of bedbugs killed every day has been more than forty or fifty. In total, I have eliminated about fifty or sixty thousand, but I am still bitten all over, my body is covered in wounds, and I can't sleep peacefully for a single night! I remember once I went to a certain newspaper office to visit a friend, sat for five minutes, and when I was about to leave, I took my long gown from the coat hook on the wall, only to see that a dozen or twenty ambitious bedbugs had been added to the collar and sleeves. The number of bedbugs in Shanghai is truly shocking, which is something that the inland cannot match! Fortunately, bedbugs have always been called "rich bugs," and they are full of the spirit of gold, silver, wine, and meat. Perhaps the reason why bedbugs are so numerous is precisely because they are endowed with spiritual energy, and it is not a loss to be a place of outstanding people. If there were more white lice that Wang Meng scratched while sitting and unbuttoning his clothes, it would be too shabby and would inevitably become a stain on this prosperous land, greatly embarrassing the people of Shanghai!

I call bedbugs "Nanjing bugs." In the past, the saying often went, "Nanjing has three many: many bedbugs, many donkeys, and many expectant officials." It can be seen that Nanjing's bedbugs have long been famous both at home and abroad and appreciated by all! However, since it was changed to the new capital, the atmosphere has been completely renewed, and the past is very different from the present. Donkeys and expectant officials have both disappeared and long become historical relics. I only don't know how the rise and fall of bedbugs is, whether they also have a little sense of vicissitudes? I have not lived in Nanjing, and I don't know how the bedbugs in Nanjing compare to those in Shanghai. Are they "brothers in the policies of Lu and Wei" or "like a small wizard seeing a great wizard"? I dare not speculate or make a rash judgment as to which is superior, but I believe that the bedbugs in Nanjing, at most, will not be more numerous than in Shanghai, and the bedbugs in Shanghai, at a minimum, will certainly not be less numerous than in Nanjing. I would like to ask a few statistical experts who have lived in both Beijing and Shanghai for a long time to use their experience and insights to honestly review and compare them! It's just that bedbugs are not called "Shanghai bugs" but are called "Nanjing bugs." Is this the good fortune of Shanghai, or the misfortune of bedbugs?

Since last year, Shanghai has added another kind of insect, only slightly less numerous than bedbugs, which is the dung beetle that rolls dung into balls everywhere, driving them away to no avail, and also a major problem for Shanghai residents. "Where did they come from and gather here?" Everyone is racking their brains to figure out the reason for their sudden procreation, but someone checked the ancient books and thought that the saying "there are those who pursue the stench on the sea" had long existed, so no wonder "things gather by type, and they share the same stink"! Is that so?

Swapped Phoenixes 184

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Seven: High Fraternal Affection Hides Letters and Pities Weak Sister; Heavy Air of Poetry and Books Peeks at Shadow Laughing at Cold Scholar

Wu Xuan looked at him, still very distressed. He himself was stunned and thought for a while. At this time, he saw that Menglan's bangs covered her long eyebrows. He couldn't see what her eyes were like. He nodded a few times and said: Let's go, I'll send you back. Menglan didn't say anything, and quietly followed her brother home. When Wu Xuan arrived at the door, he whispered: I won't go in, you be as usual. Although Menglan received such an exhortation, she still had a knot in her heart. At noon, she felt even more uneasy, so she broke the rule and took the initiative to go to Li Youmei's house to talk to him. Unexpectedly, when she arrived at Li's house, their maid gave a very tempting reply, saying that he had gone to a relative's house, the Zhang family. Menglan thought for a while, did not want to wait, and returned disappointed. What Li's maid said was true. Youmei was also a little doubtful why Menglan seemed a little uncomfortable when she talked about Zhang Litian. Although he didn't say anything, he could see the clues if he went to Zhang Litian's house to take a closer look. With this in mind, he brought a little ordinary socializing from his family and came to Zhang's house alone. On this day, the weather at noon was very promising for summer. Youmei held a cloth umbrella and walked on the road, as if feeling a heat wave rising from the ground and attacking people's bodies. When she arrived at the Zhang family, the two old trees in their courtyard made half a courtyard of cool shade. Although some sunlight was revealed in the leaves and scattered on the moss-dotted brick ground, making white patterns, there was a cool breeze blowing on people, naturally clearing and cooling people's troubled minds. Youmei put away the cloth umbrella and stood in the courtyard, first calling out "Aunt." Mrs. Zhang felt that such long summer days should not be wasted. She held a piece of old clothes and slowly sewed it under the window, where there was a cool breeze. Turning her head and seeing that it was Youmei, she called out "Miss Li" and welcomed her into the courtyard. She smiled and said: Sit in the hall? Or sit in the room? Female students are not afraid of people. The hall is cooler, so sit in the hall. When Youmei arrived in the hall, her eyes were already shooting around. She saw a lacquered bamboo curtain hanging outside the door of Guoqi's room. It was not very clear to see from outside the curtain, but she faintly smelled a scent of sandalwood coming from inside the curtain, and she could not see a trace of smoke between the inside and outside. Because she said: Aunt's house is clean everywhere. Answer with seat (87)

Yarn Flower Speculation Brings Unexpected Surprises, Yarn Market Wildly Rises and Plunges, Monthly Peak Reaches 38 Yuan, Shorts Heavily Add to Positions in Distant Months, Near-Term Rises 8 Yuan, Distant-Term Falls Approximately 5 Yuan, Spot Sales Stagnant Due to High Prices 185

Recently, the yarn and cloth market and the yarn flower market have been turbulent. General speculators are extremely hot and restless. With sudden rises and falls, the trend is chaotic. Both large longs and shorts have considerable opposing force. Trading is prosperous. Therefore, it rises on one session and falls on the second, and the momentum is fierce, making it difficult to resist. Initially, the upward trend of the October contract reached the limit on the previous day. Checking the actual chips, there were still 12,000 bales remaining. The shorts rushed to cover, jumping 10 yuan to 238 yuan. Because its upward momentum was too激, it was not far from the spot yarn price. Also, because the spot yarn asking price was too high, the customers were sluggish. Thus, the popularity gradually calmed down. The November contract had a gentle upward force, rising only 3.1 yuan. The remaining distant contracts fell sharply by 3.5 yuan. It was said that the Qingdao yarn market fell by more than 10 yuan, and it was also said that foreign firms were selling. In fact, the price has reached a high level. The momentum is certain. The longs took the opportunity to take profits and挫. In the afternoon, it still changed uncertainly. According to market observations, most of the floating shorts have closed out. The market price has soared by more than 30 yuan. Although the longs continue to猛抬, there may be temporary reactions. How the future will be depends on the actual needs for transference.

Floating Longs and Scattered Shorts Have Been Concluded

At the opening of the standard yarn market, the current month rose sharply by 10 yuan to 238 yuan due to the previous day's limit up, and the shorts were extremely panicked. The November contract rose more slowly, rising by 3.1 yuan. The distant month suddenly became tired, falling by 3.5 yuan. Although the spot yarn price is high, sales are sluggish because the price is too high. Thus, the shorts heavily sold in the distant month, and the floating longs concluded their positions. The market then turned sharply downward. In the second session, the near-month also declined. As a result, the current month rose by 4.5 yuan from the previous day's closing price, and the distant month fell by 1.9 yuan to 5.2 yuan. In the afternoon, the market opened again at 4 o'clock. The current month continued to fall by 1.6 yuan, but the distant month was slightly stronger. Unexpectedly, 1,600 bales of the 38th contract in the current month were purchased, and the price jumped 7.1 yuan, reaching 38 yuan again. The remaining months also rose by 1.7 yuan to 3.1 yuan, but the last two months were unchanged. It is said that the shorts continued to sell in the distant months. In the third session, the current month suddenly fell by 2.2 yuan, and the distant month also fell by 1.2, 3, and 5 jiao. The closing prices of each month rebounded slightly. As a result, the current month rose another 2.5 yuan from the morning closing price, the November contract rose another 2 yuan, and the distant contract rose or fell by 2 or 3 jiao. The market closed at 7:30. Finance 193

Empty Side Takes Advantage of High Prices to Increase Bets. Standard Gold Bar Price Rises then Falls Back. Trading Started Above Sixty Yuan. Result: A Reversal and a Drop of 1.1 Yuan.

Yesterday, the gold market saw pure gold continue to rise. The opening price immediately broke through the sixty-yuan mark. Large short sellers increased their positions, and buying momentum gradually dissipated. As a result, the market turned downward. In the morning, overseas silver markets showed a contraction in London and stability in the US. Forward silver prices in Monte Carlo contracted by between 4.5 and 5 fen. Exchange rates all contracted. Spot gold in London rose by two pence. Preliminary off-exchange trading opened and immediately rose to around sixty yuan. The Central Bank's listed exchange rates showed stability in both British and American currencies. The Customs Gold Unit rose by three li. The standard gold bar price was listed at 1157 yuan and 8 jiao. Wanxing Hengchang Yongda Decheng Hengyu and others actively purchased, leading to a gradual increase. A high opening price was recorded in the morning. After the opening, major players took advantage of the high prices to sell off, immediately dropping the price back below the sixty-yuan mark. However, there were many buyers active at the lower prices, causing a rebound. HSBC's listed exchange rates showed stability and strength in both British and American currencies, leading long positions to also close out. The silver balancing tax was announced to have contracted by half a fen, continuing the downward trend. Although there was some fluctuation in the middle, the trend remained weak at noon. In the afternoon, long positions took the opportunity to close out, leading to a continued weakening of the opening price. HSBC's forward rates remained soft. Support was maintained at the lower prices, leading to a temporary rise, but the buying momentum was weak and unsustainable. In the end, the market remained depressed. Here is a record of the market conditions for the day.

The opening price in the morning was 1160 yuan and 6 jiao, an increase of 1 yuan and 2 jiao compared to the previous close. Dadecheng Fuxing Yongshou's long positions fell from 7 jiao to 59 yuan and 8 jiao. Yuxin Xiang Wanxing Dadecheng Yuanmao Yongding Kanglian closed out their positions. Lifeng Jingfu Dachangxiang, although selling, experienced slight fluctuations. HSBC's listed exchange rates showed stability in both British and American currencies, rising to 60 yuan and 6 jiao. Lifeng Yuanheng Yongde Dingkang continuously sold off. The silver balancing tax fell slightly by half a fen, dropping to 59 yuan and 4 jiao. Dadecheng Wanxing closed out long positions at the lower prices, rising to 60 yuan and 1 jiao. Qiafeng Yong Yuanmao, Yong still had sales, falling back to 59 yuan and 1 jiao. Short covering led to a later rally. The noon closing price was 1159 yuan and 3 jiao.

The afternoon market opened at 1158 yuan and 9 jiao. Yuanmao, Yongda Heng sold positions, falling to 8 yuan and 5 jiao. Zhengchang Dadecheng Hengchang Yong purchased actively, gradually rising to 9 yuan and 1 jiao. Fuxing Yong Yuanmao Yongxiangfeng and others sold off. By the close, the price had fallen to 1158 yuan and 3 jiao. The closing price was weak and flat.

The closing price, based on the Central Bank's standard gold bar buying rate, was 1157 yuan and 8 jiao, approximately half a yuan higher than the closing price. The current month's registered price was 1155 yuan, November's was 1157 yuan, and December's was 1159 yuan. The morning replenishment was 1155 yuan, and refined gold, together with the additional 6 yuan, was 1166 yuan and 6 jiao. The spot market was stable. Tianjin goods, with an additional 1 yuan and 5 jiao, saw Shengyuan Yong sell 140 taels. Hachi, through Tongfeng Hengda Fengheng, sold a small quantity with an additional 12 yuan and 5 jiao. The buying price, with an additional 8 yuan, was the transaction price.

For the November to December futures spread, the long side, Shenkang, posted 119 contracts. Dingkang posted 105 contracts. Chunyuan Yong paid in 1 yuan and 4 jiao. Yuanmao Yong paid Dadecheng 14 contracts, Yuanheng paid Dadecheng 49 contracts, and Hengyu paid 21 contracts, all at 2 yuan and 4 jiao.

Trading within the market was average. In summary, Fuyu Xiang Yuanmao, Yongsu Xinxiang Dadecheng Yida Wan and Tongfeng Heng Zhengchang Hengchang Yong Tongtaichang and others were on the buying side. Qiafeng Yong Lifeng Fuyu Yong Shunmao Dingkang Yuanheng Hengyu Shengyuan Yong Qingfa Yongda Heng and others were on the selling side. Xiangfeng Shenda Yong Yuanmao Yong Dadecheng and others were early buyers and later sellers.

The day's market conditions were initially stable but later weakened. The morning opening price was 1160 yuan and 6 jiao. The later closing price was 258 yuan and 3 jiao. The highest price was 1160 yuan and 7 jiao, and the lowest price was 1158 yuan and 3 jiao, a fluctuation of 2 yuan and 4 jiao. The result was a drop of 1 yuan and 1 jiao compared to the previous close. 280 contracts remained for the current month, and 2779 contracts remained for November. In total, there were eight long parties and thirteen short parties. There were 6272 contracts for December futures, with 39 long parties and 27 short parties. The total transaction volume was 2583 contracts in the morning session and 546 contracts in the afternoon session.

Yesterday, the foreign exchange market saw a contraction in exchange rates, with British currency stable and US currency tight, experiencing fluctuations in the middle. Securities - Bond Market Rises, Both Long and Short Sides Are Swapping, Market Price Rises Five Cents to Six Jiao 195

Yesterday at the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange, the market started well but then faltered. There was no clear performance in the market, and it remained volatile and uncertain. Both long and short sides of the market had their own opinions and perspectives. Therefore, the market price rose and then fell, without any firm signs. Most transactions in the market were swaps, and very few new buy-sell orders were executed. The future prospects remain uncertain and volatile. Yesterday's trading saw active buying of numbers 32 and 45, as well as by various individual investors. Only number 5 saw more selling, with high prices rising sharply, by between 1 jiao and 5 fen to 6 jiao and 5 fen. The final trading became weak, and transactions were also thin, mostly down by 5 fen to 1 jiao. The afternoon opening saw more swap transactions, with number 52 seeing significant selling. Except for the A and B types of current month contracts, which rose slightly by 5 fen, the rest continued to fall by 5 fen, 1 jiao, or 3 jiao. The closing price was still volatile and uncertain, with long and short positions swapping, taking different positions, and the market price fluctuating up and down. Grain - Flour Price Sets New Record 196

Yesterday, the flour market saw prices rise across all months, setting a new record. Before the abolition of the tael and the adoption of the yuan, the highest price was 2 taels, 6 qian, and 8 fen. Today, the forward price has reached 3 yuan and 8 jiao, equivalent to 2 taels, 7 qian, and 3 or 4 fen. Therefore, the current situation is extraordinary. It is said that the harvest this year is abundant, but this phenomenon is inevitable. It is unknown how those advocating for exports will manage the aftermath. At the beginning, the market felt calm because foreign wheat quotations had decreased slightly by about 4 jiao. However, large players outside the industry, due to various reasons, made every effort to push prices up, resulting in brisk trading, with 700,000 to 800,000 bags traded in half a day. The market also rose by 2 to 4 jiao and 4 fen. When the afternoon session opened, short positions in the current month, due to its proximity to delivery, were aggressively covered by both industry insiders and outsiders, leading to a surge in the market. Although market sentiment was also high for forward months, factories continued to sell to hedge, and stability was seen amid the firm trend. The repeated increases at present may lead to significant reversals in the future when prices approach those of foreign wheat.

Futures Wheat Entirely Speculative 197

Yesterday, the futures wheat market opened strong in the morning, then stabilized, and then rose again. Initially, due to the anticipation of a large jump in recent cotton yarn prices by outside players, market sentiment was also high when prices opened, with both near and far terms rising by 5, 6, or 7 fen. Then, industry insiders, due to foreign wheat declining for two consecutive days, sold off their floating positions, causing market sentiment to gradually decline, falling back by 3 fen compared to the opening price. When the afternoon session opened, trading in the near term was quiet, and prices did not fluctuate much. Due to the resurgence of the flour market, prices rose by 2 or 3 fen. In February and March, due to active buying by outsiders, prices rose by 5 or 6 fen. In the current situation, there is no longer any reason or logic, and it is purely speculative. The supply of current wheat is very scarce, and sellers continue to raise prices. Yesterday, high-quality wagon wheat opened at 5 yuan and 5 jiao and a half, which was more expensive by nearly 1 jiao, but factories disliked the high price and unreliable quality, so their interest waned. Only Shen Dacheng traded a few hundred bags for the whole day.

Yesterday, although the early indica rice market was strong, southern routes were smoother, and market sentiment progressed accordingly. Cantonese merchants focused on coarse indica rice, and the market for coarse indica rice became tighter as daily arrivals were fewer. Yesterday, the market rose sharply by 1 jiao to 1 jiao and a half. Milled rice was traded smoothly in Shantou, and there were also inquiries from the North, so the market also moved upward, with prices rising gradually by 5 or 6 fen to about 1 jiao. Yuan rice, broken rice, and rice bran only rose by 3 to 5 fen. Yesterday, 6900 bags of Jiangxi rice, 3637 bags of Hunan rice, 1220 bags of Taiwanese indica rice, and 176 bags of Beijing coarse rice were sold.

Mourning Mr. Lu Xun 212

— Li Yinfei

"People should indeed live, but for the sake of evolution; it is okay to suffer, but for the sake of eliminating all future suffering; and even more so, one should fight, but for the sake of reform. … If one does not utter a word, nor fire a single arrow at the main force of darkness, and only babbles incessantly at the 'weak,' then even if he appears righteous, I cannot help but say… I really cannot bear it anymore… he is indeed an accomplice to murder." (Lu Xun: On the Affairs of Mrs. Qin Liqi)

From the May Fourth Movement to the present, Mr. Lu Xun has been fighting the "main force of darkness" at all times. The champions of the May Fourth era have either retired or joined the enemy's camp, while Mr. Lu Xun has not been eliminated by the times. For the sake of human "evolution," and for the sake of "eliminating all future suffering," he stands at the forefront of the times, bravely and steadfastly "fighting" the "main force of darkness," and although he is "suffering," he considers it acceptable.

Because he is always a warrior standing at the forefront of the times, old age is not only harmless to him but also beneficial. When other "old generals" cannot withstand the rapid current of the times and fall, or try to hold on to the times so that they can stand firm, Mr. Lu Xun learns richer experiences in the rapids. These experiences are lacking or even non-existent to other young warriors.

Therefore, this seasoned old warrior is even more worthy of our love and support. But who would have expected that this vanguard of the times would not be able to withstand his physiological weakness and leave his troubled country!

Mr. Lu Xun has been ill a lot in the past two years, but even in his illness, he seems to have never thought about his own body. On the contrary, he worked even harder. In a miscellany called "Death," he said:

"Since last year, every year after recovering from illness, while lying on a rattan chair, I cannot help but think about what I should do after my strength recovers: what articles to write, what books to translate or publish. After deciding, I conclude: That's it. — But I must hurry. This thought of 'must hurry' is something I didn't have before, because unconsciously, I remembered my age. But I have never directly thought about 'death.'"

Under such efforts, in the past two years, books such as "Dead Souls," "Lace Literature," and many essays scattered in various publications have appeared. And because of this, his body became weaker and weaker, and finally could not withstand the attack of illness and closed his eyes forever. If he could have thought a little more about his own body and rested well before his sick body had fully recovered, I think he wouldn't have died now, would he? However, in order to "eliminate all future suffering," he thought about many things to do before his strength had recovered, and "must hurry" to do them. In a way, this is self-hastening one's death, but who is it for after all?

In his will, he said: "Do not do anything about commemoration." And he said, "Forget me and take care of your own life. — If not? Then it's really foolish." Such a warrior has died, and it is really not easy for us to forget him lightly. And "do not do anything about commemoration," in form, we may be able to do it, but in our hearts, we often "commemorate" because it is not easy to forget. When "taking care of our own lives," when reading his posthumous works, we cannot help but "commemorate" him, because the biggest problem in China today, the problem shared by everyone, is the problem of national survival, and all aspects of life (including eating and sleeping) are related to this problem; for example, eating may not be related to love, but currently, the eating and love of Chinese people are somewhat related to the advantages and disadvantages of ××. This can be understood by looking at the situation in Manchuria and North China." (See Mr. Lu Xun's response to questions from visitors during his illness, "On Our Current Literary Movement.") Thus, even "do not do anything about commemoration" seems unlikely.

Naturally, Mr. Lu Xun's reason for saying this is very clear: because he does not want people to be foolish, he tells them to "take care of their own lives" and not to commemorate him. But here, we can see that to "take care of our own lives," one can only follow Mr. Lu Xun's path (although there are different ways to go). And on the long journey, it is impossible and unnecessary to forget the partners who have traveled the same road.

An unfortunate piece of news pierced the hearts of many young people of the era. The newspaper reported to us: "The giant of the Chinese literary world," "Mr. Lu Xun is dead"!
